TOOLKIT & METHODOLOGY\n\n## 3.1 TOOL SELECTION PRINCIPLES\n\n- IMAGE TOOL PRIORITY:\n  * For any request involving image creation, modification, style change, or visual design, ALWAYS prefer the Image Tool.\n  * Do NOT describe images purely in text when an image output is expected.\n  * If an image result is required, the Image Tool is mandatory.\n\n- CLI TOOLS PREFERENCE:\n  * Always prefer CLI tools over Python scripts when possible\n  * CLI tools are generally faster and more efficient for:\n    1. Synchronous Commands (blocking):\n      * You can omit `blocking`, as it defaults to true\n      * Use for quick operations that complete within 60 seconds\n      * Commands run directly and wait for completion\n      * Example:\n        <function_calls>\n        <execute-command session_name="default" blocking="true">\n        ls -l\n        </execute-command>\n        </function_calls>\n        (or simply omit the blocking parameter as it defaults to true)\n      * IMPORTANT: Do not use for long-running operations as they will timeout after 60 seconds\n\n  2. Asynchronous Commands (non-blocking):\n      * Use `blocking="false"` for any command that might take longer than 60 seconds or for starting background services\n      * Commands run in background and return immediately\n      * Example:\n        <function_calls>\n        <execute-command session_name="dev" blocking="false">\n        npm run dev\n        </execute-command>\n        </function_calls>\n      * Common use cases:\n        - Development servers (Next.js, React, etc.)\n        - Build processes\n        - Long-running data processing\n        - Background services\n\n- Session Management:\n  * Each command must specify a session_name\n  * Use consistent session names for related commands\n  * Different sessions are isolated from each other\n  * Example: Use "build" session for build commands, "dev" for development servers\n  * Sessions maintain state between commands\n\n- Command Execution Guidelines:\n  * For commands that might take longer than 60 seconds, ALWAYS use run_async="true"\n  * Do not rely on increasing timeout for long-running commands\n  * Use proper session names for organization\n  * Chain commands with && for sequential execution\n  * Use | for piping output between commands\n  * Redirect output to files for long-running processes\n\n- Avoid commands requiring confirmation; actively use -y or -f flags for automatic confirmation\n- Avoid commands with excessive output; save to files when necessary\n- Chain multiple commands with operators to minimize interruptions and improve efficiency:\n  1. Use && for sequential execution: `command1 && command2 && command3`\n  2. Use || for fallback execution: `command1 || command2`\n  3. Use ; for unconditional execution: `command1; command2`\n  4. Use | for piping output: `command1 | command2`\n  5. Use > and >> for output redirection: `command > file` or `command >> file`\n- Use pipe operator to pass command outputs, simplifying operations\n- Use non-interactive `bc` for simple calculations, Python for complex math; never calculate mentally\n- Use `uptime` command when users explicitly request sandbox status check or wake-up\n\n## 3.3 CODE DEVELOPMENT PRACTICES\n- CODING:\n  * Must save code to files before execution; direct code input to interpreter commands is forbidden\n  * Write Python code for complex mathematical calculations and analysis\n  * Use search tools to find solutions when encountering unfamiliar problems\n  * For index.html, use deployment tools directly, or package everything into a zip file and provide it as a message attachment\n  * When creating web interfaces, always create CSS files first before HTML to ensure proper styling and design consistency\n  * For images, use real image URLs from sources like unsplash.com, pexels.com, pixabay.com, giphy.com, or wikimedia.org instead of creating placeholder images; use placeholder.com only as a last resort\n\n- WEBSITE DEPLOYMENT:\n  * Only use the \'deploy\' tool when users explicitly request permanent deployment to a production environment\n  * The deploy tool publishes static HTML+CSS+JS sites to a public URL using S3 web Pages\n  * If the same name is used for deployment, it will redeploy to the same project as before\n  * For temporary or development purposes, serve files locally instead of using the deployment tool\n  * When editing HTML files, always share the preview URL provided by the automatically running HTTP server with the user\n  * The preview URL is automatically generated and available in the tool results when creating or editing HTML files\n  * When deploying, ensure all assets (images, scripts, stylesheets) use relative paths to work correctly\n\n- PYTHON EXECUTION: Create reusable modules with proper error handling and logging. Use -nopgbrk to remove page breaks\n  2. pdfinfo: Get PDF metadata\n    - Use to check PDF properties\n    - Extract page count and dimensions\n  3. pdfimages: Extract images from PDFs\n    - Use -j to convert to JPEG\n    - Use for text replacement\n    - Use for pattern matching\n- File Analysis:\n  1. file: Determine file type\n  2. wc: Count words/lines\n  3. head/tail: View file parts\n  4. less: View large files\n- Data Processing:\n  1. jq: JSON processing\n    - Use -n to specify number of lines\n    - Use -f to follow file changes\n  3. awk: Pattern scanning and processing\n    - Use for column-based data processing\n    - Use for complex text transformations\n  4. find: Locate files and directories\n    - Use for precise text matching\n  2. Combine with CLI tools for powerful searches\n  3. Save complex patterns to files for reuse\n  4. Test patterns with small samples first\n  5. Each section contains specific, actionable subtasks based on complexity - use only as many as needed, no more\n3. Each task should be specific, actionable, and have clear completion criteria\n4. MUST actively work through these tasks one by one, checking them off as completed\n5. Adapt the plan as needed while maintaining its integrity as your execution compass\n\n## 5.2 TODO.MD FILE STRUCTURE AND USAGE\nThe todo.md file is your primary working document and action plan:\n\n1. Contains the complete list of tasks you MUST complete to fulfill the user\'s request\n2. Format with clear sections, each containing specific tasks marked with [ ] (incomplete) or [x] (complete)\n3. Each task should be specific, actionable, and have clear completion criteria\n4. MUST actively work through these tasks one by one, checking them off as completed\n5. Before every action, consult your todo.md to determine which task to tackle next\n6. The todo.md serves as your instruction set - if a task is in todo.md, you are responsible for completing it\n7. Update the todo.md as you make progress, adding new tasks as needed and marking completed ones\n8. Never delete tasks from todo.md - instead mark them complete with [x] to maintain a record of your work\n9. Once ALL tasks in todo.md are marked complete [x], you MUST call either the \'complete\' state or \'ask\' tool to signal task completion\n10. SCOPE CONSTRAINT: Focus on completing existing tasks before adding new ones; avoid continuously expanding scope\n11. CAPABILITY AWARENESS: Only add tasks that are achievable with your available tools and capabilities\n12. FINALITY: After marking a section complete, do not reopen it or add new tasks unless explicitly directed by the user\n13. STOPPING CONDITION: If you\'ve made 3 consecutive updates to todo.md without completing any tasks, reassess your approach and either simplify your plan or **use the \'ask\' tool to seek user guidance.**\n14. COMPLETION VERIFICATION: Only mark a task as [x] complete when you have concrete evidence of completion\n15. SIMPLICITY: Keep your todo.md lean and direct with clear actions, avoiding unnecessary verbosity or granularity\n\n## 5.3 EXECUTION PHILOSOPHY\nYour approach is deliberately methodical and persistent:\n\n1. Operate in a continuous loop until explicitly stopped\n2. Execute one step at a time, following a consistent loop: evaluate state → select tool → execute → provide narrative update → track progress\n3. Every action is guided by your todo.md, consulting it before selecting any tool\n4. Thoroughly verify each completed step before moving forward\n5. **Provide Markdown-formatted narrative updates directly in your responses** to keep the user informed of your progress, explain your thinking, and clarify the next steps. Use headers, brief descriptions, and context to make your process transparent.\n6. CRITICALLY IMPORTANT: Continue running in a loop until either:\n  - Using the **\'ask\' tool (THE ONLY TOOL THE USER CAN RESPOND TO)** to wait for essential user input (this pauses the loop)\n  - Using the \'complete\' tool when ALL tasks are finished\n7. For casual conversation:\n  - Use **\'ask\'** to properly end the conversation and wait for user input (**USER CAN RESPOND**)\n8. For tasks:\n  - Use **\'ask\'** when you need essential user input to proceed (**USER CAN RESPOND**)\n  - Provide **narrative updates** frequently in your responses to keep the user informed without requiring their input\n  - Use \'complete\' only when ALL tasks are finished\n9. MANDATORY COMPLETION:\n  - IMMEDIATELY use \'complete\' or \'ask\' after ALL tasks in todo.md are marked [x]\n  - NO additional commands or verifications after all tasks are complete\n  - NO further exploration or information gathering after completion\n  - NO redundant checks or validations after completion\n  - FAILURE to use \'complete\' or \'ask\' after task completion is a critical error\n\n## 5.4 TASK MANAGEMENT CYCLE\n1. STATE EVALUATION: Examine Todo.md for priorities, analyze recent Tool Results for environment understanding, and review past actions for context\n2. TOOL SELECTION: Choose exactly one tool that advances the current todo item\n3. EXECUTION: Wait for tool execution and observe results\n4. **NARRATIVE UPDATE:** Provide a **Markdown-formatted** narrative update directly in your response before the next tool call. Include explanations of what you\'ve done, what you\'re about to do, and why. Use headers, brief paragraphs, and formatting to enhance readability.\n5. PROGRESS TRACKING: Update todo.md with completed items and new tasks\n6. METHODICAL ITERATION: Repeat until section completion\n7. SECTION TRANSITION: Document completion and move to next section\n8. COMPLETION: IMMEDIATELY use \'complete\' or \'ask\' when ALL tasks are finished\n\n# 6. CONTENT CREATION\n\n## 6.1 WRITING GUIDELINES\n- Write content in continuous paragraphs using varied sentence lengths for engaging prose; avoid list formatting\n- Use prose and paragraphs by default; BROWSER AUTOMATION TOOLS\n\n- BROWSER CONTROL: All browser interaction goes through `browser-tool <action> [args...]` via `execute-command`.\n  * The browser (Chromium) is already running. Each command connects, acts, observes, and disconnects.\n\n- WORKFLOW (observe-act loop):\n  1. Run an action (e.g. navigate, click, fill). The tool automatically observes the page after every action.\n  2. Read the output: URL, title, interactive elements list, accessibility tree, and screenshot path.\n  3. Reference elements by their `[index]` number from the elements list (e.g. `click "[3]"`).\n  4. Use `see-image` on the screenshot path when you need to verify visual layout or images.\n\n- AVAILABLE COMMANDS:\n  * `observe` - View current page state without acting\n  * `navigate <url>` - Go to a URL\n  * `click <selector>` - Click an element (use `[N]` for element index, or CSS selector)\n  * `fill <selector> <text>` - Clear a field and fill it with text\n  * `type <selector> <text>` - Type text character by character\n  * `press <key>` - Press a key (Enter, Tab, Escape, etc.)\n  * `select <selector> <value>` - Select a dropdown option\n  * `scroll_down [px]` / `scroll_up [px]` - Scroll (default 500px)\n  * `scroll_to_text <text>` - Scroll until text is visible\n  * `go_back` - Navigate back\n  * `wait [seconds]` - Wait (default 2s)\n  * `extract_text [selector]` - Extract text content from page or element\n  * `extract_links [selector]` - Extract all links\n  * `screenshot [filename]` - Take a manual screenshot\n  * `dismiss_overlay` - Dismiss cookie banners or modals\n  * `js <script>` - Execute JavaScript on the page\n\n- CAPTCHA / HUMAN ASSISTANCE: If you encounter a CAPTCHA, verification, or any situation where automated interaction is stuck, MUST use `web-browser-takeover` to hand control to the user.\n\n# 12. CHAT MODE AND AGENTIC MODE\n\n## Mode Detection (STRICT)\n\nYour mode is determined EXCLUSIVELY by system-reminder messages:\n- If the LATEST system-reminder explicitly says "chat mode" is active → CHAT MODE\n- Otherwise → AGENTIC MODE (this is the DEFAULT)\n\n**NEVER infer chat mode from context.** Using `ask` recently, casual conversation, or simple user questions are NOT indicators of chat mode. = views_str.lower().replace(\',\', \'\').strip()\n    match = re.match(r\'([\\d.]+)\\s*([km]?)\', views_str)\n    if match:\n        num = float(match.group(1))\n        multiplier = match.group(2)\n        if multiplier == \'m\':\n            return int(num * 1_000_000)\n        elif multiplier == \'k\':\n            return int(num * 1_000)\n        return int(num)\n    return 0\n\ndef analyze_dataset(filepath, ingredient_name):\n    """Analyze a YouTube dataset"""\n    with open(filepath, \'r\', encoding=\'utf-8\') as f:\n        data = json.load(f)\n    \n    videos = seconds)\n        elif len(parts) == 3:\n            hours, minutes, seconds = int(parts[0]), int(parts[1]), int(parts[2])\n            durations.append(hours * 3600 + minutes * 60 + seconds)\n    \n After the World War II, ozone production has  increased again.\\\\r\\\\n   4:224 minutes, 22 seconds But today, chlorine is more preferable   to ozone for water disinfection,  yet the scientists still working  \\\\r\\\\n   4:284 minutes, 28 secondson research about alternative disinfection  as there was once in 1973, popped up the   discovery of trihalomethanes (THM) as a harmful  disinfection byproduct of chlorine disinfection.\\\\r\\\\n   Chapter 3: Ozone Process\\\\r\\\\n   4:444 minutes, 44 secondsNext, let\\\\u2019s move on to the ozonation process.  The formation of oxygen into ozone occurs with  \\\\r\\\\n   4:514 minutes, 51 secondsthe use of energy. This process is carried  out by an electric discharge field as in the  \\\\r\\\\n   4:574 minutes, 57 secondsCD-type ozone generator which is corona discharge  simulation of the lightning, or by the ultraviolet  \\\\r\\\\n   5:065 minutes, 6 secondsradiation as in UV-type ozone generator which is  a simulation of the ultraviolet rays from the sun.  \\\\r\\\\n   5:145 minutes, 14 secondsIn addition to these commercial methods, ozone  may also be made through electrolytic and chemical   reactions. In general, an ozonation  system includes passing dry clean air  \\\\r\\\\n   5:255 minutes, 25 secondsto a high voltage electric discharge. In treating  small quantities of waste, the UV ozonation is the  \\\\r\\\\n   5:345 minutes, 34 secondsmost common while large-scale systems use either  corona discharge or other bulk ozone-producing  \\\\r\\\\n   5:395 minutes, 39 secondsmethods.So let\\\'s move on to the process, ozone  generator will produce ozone. Then, ozone  \\\\r\\\\n   5:465 minutes, 46 secondsinjector will creates micro bubbles which will  increased the stability of ozone in groundwater.  \\\\r\\\\n   5:535 minutes, 53 secondsAfter that, ozone is dissolved in water at the  storage tank which will produce highly ozonated  \\\\r\\\\n   6:006 minuteswater that is used to control bacteria and water  is being treated. Since the ozone will react with   metals to create insoluble metal oxides, post  filtration is required before entering the house.\\\\r\\\\n   Chapter 4: Advantages Disadvantages\\\\r\\\\n   6:146 minutes, 14 secondsAdvantages and disadvantages of ozone in water  treatment.When looking at the ozonation process,  \\\\r\\\\n   6:226 minutes, 22 secondsthere are numerous advantages that come with  using this process to purify water, which include  \\\\r\\\\n   6:286 minutes, 28 secondsthe treatment process occurs without adding  any kind of chemicals to the water. Besides,  \\\\r\\\\n   6:346 minutes, 34 secondsozonation eliminates many impurities in the water;  as well as a wide variety of inorganic, organic  \\\\r\\\\n   6:416 minutes, 41 secondsand microbiological problems. Also, ozone is a  very strong oxidizing power with a short reaction  \\\\r\\\\n   6:486 minutes, 48 secondstime thus requires significantly less contact  time to remove inorganic and organic compounds.  \\\\r\\\\n   6:546 minutes, 54 secondsHowever, there are also numerous disadvantages  of ozonation that we should take into account,  \\\\r\\\\n   7:007 minuteswhich include the operation and equipment  costs for ozonation are relatively high and  \\\\r\\\\n   7:067 minutes, 6 secondsrequire consistent maintenance. Next, ozone  is less soluble in water compared to chlorine  \\\\r\\\\n   7:137 minutes, 13 secondsand therefore special mixing techniques will need  to be used in order to dissolve properly. message\\\\n\\\\n[Skip to main content](#content)\\\\n\\\\nGuidance\\\\n\\\\n# Bottled drinking water: how to produce and label\\\\n\\\\nHow to register as a producer, and the rules you must follow to produce and market bottled drinking water.\\\\n\\\\nFrom:\\\\n:   [Department for Environment, Food & Rural Affairs](/government/organisations/department-for-environment-food-rural-affairs)\\\\n\\\\nPublished\\\\n:   28 May 2020\\\\n\\\\nGet emails about this page\\\\n\\\\n## Applies to England\\\\n\\\\n* [Guidance for Northern Ireland and Wales](https://www.food.gov.uk/document/guidance-on-natural-mineral-water-spring-water-and-bottled-drinking-water-regulations-in-wales-and-northern-ireland)\\\\n* [Guidance for Scotland](https://www.foodstandards.gov.scot/contact-us)\\\\n\\\\nPrint this page\\\\n\\\\nThis guide is for people or businesses who want to market their bottled drinking water in England.\\\\n\\\\nTo market in:\\\\n\\\\n* Wales or Northern Ireland, read [Food Standards Agency guidance](https://www.food.gov.uk/document/guidance-on-natural-mineral-water-spring-water-and-bottled-drinking-water-regulations-in-wales-and-northern-ireland)\\\\n* Scotland, contact [Food Standards Scotland](https://www.foodstandards.gov.scot/contact-us)\\\\n\\\\n## What counts as bottled drinking water\\\\n\\\\nBottled drinking water is any bottled water that\\\\u2019s not labelled or sold as:\\\\n\\\\n* [natural mineral water](https://www.gov.uk/guidance/natural-mineral-water-how-to-produce-and-label)\\\\n* [spring water](https://www.gov.uk/guidance/spring-water-how-to-produce-and-label)\\\\n\\\\nIt\\\\u2019s also sometimes known as table water.\\\\n\\\\nYou can bottle this water from any source, including public and private water sources, as long as:\\\\n\\\\n* your water meets the rules in this guide\\\\n* you do not mislead consumers about its origin\\\\n\\\\nYou can sell it directly to consumers in bottles as well as other containers, such as:\\\\n\\\\n* tetra packs and cartons\\\\n* water coolers\\\\n* pouches\\\\n\\\\nYou do not need to state the composition of the water on the label.\\\\n\\\\nYou\\\\u2019re allowed to use any treatment, and you do not need to list treatments on your labelling.\\\\n\\\\nCheck the [different types of bottled water](https://www.gov.uk/guidance/compare-types-of-bottled-water) if you\\\\u2019re not sure which type you have.\\\\n\\\\nYou can also check if your water is exempt from the rules.\\\\n\\\\n## Steps to get registered to produce bottled drinking water\\\\n\\\\n1. Apply to [register your business](https://www.gov.uk/food-business-registration) for bottled drinking water with the local authority in the area the water is extracted from.\\\\n2. Carry out [tests](#tests) on your bottled drinking water - it must comply with limits for chemical, microbiological and radioactive substances.\\\\n3. Follow the [rules on labelling](#label) for bottled drinking water.\\\\n\\\\nThe local authority will:\\\\n\\\\n* check you\\\\u2019ve complied with all the rules\\\\n* register your business and premises for bottled drinking water\\\\n* let you know in writing when you can start producing and marketing your bottled drinking water\\\\n\\\\n## Tests you need to carry out on the water\\\\n\\\\nYou must test your bottled drinking water and make sure it complies with:\\\\n\\\\n* [chemical limits](#chemicals)\\\\n* [microbiological limits](#microbiological)\\\\n* [radioactive limits](#radioactive)\\\\n\\\\nYou need to use a [UKAS-approved laboratory](https://www.ukas.com/search-accredited-organisations), which uses recognised methods to test the water.\\\\n\\\\n### Initial and ongoing tests\\\\n\\\\nCarry out initial testing and keep records of the results - you\\\\u2019ll need to show these to the local authority. Take as many samples as you need to be sure your water complies with the rules.\\\\n\\\\nAfter initial testing, you must carry out further testing regularly. Discuss how often with the local authority you\\\\u2019re dealing with. This can vary depending on, for example, how much bottled drinking water you produce.\\\\n\\\\nFor both initial and ongoing testing, you do not need to send samples of the water to the local authority. They\\\\u2019ll carry out their own tests at your bottling plant.\\\\n\\\\n### Chemical limits\\\\n\\\\nTest your water to make sure it complies with the following limits.\\\\n\\\\nFor your initial testing, take samples at source.\\\\n\\\\n| Chemical | Maximum limit | Details |\\\\n| --- | --- | --- |\\\\n| Antimony | 5 micrograms per litre |  |\\\\n| Arsenic | 10 micrograms per litre |  |\\\\n| Benzene | 1 microgram per litre |  |\\\\n| Benzo(a)pyrene | 0.01 micrograms per litre |  |\\\\n| Boron | 1 milligram per litre |  |\\\\n| Bromate (Br03L) | 10 micrograms per litre |  |\\\\n| Cadmium | 5 micrograms per litre |  |\\\\n| Chromium | 50 micrograms per litre |  |\\\\n| Cadmium | 5 micrograms per litre |  |\\\\n| Copper | 2 milligrams per litre |  |\\\\n| Cyanide (CN) | 50 micrograms per litre |  |\\\\n| 1,2-dichloroethane | 3 micrograms per litre |  |\\\\n| Fluoride | 1.5 milligrams per litre |  |\\\\n| Lead | 10 micrograms per litre |  |\\\\n| Mercury | 1 microgram per litre |  |\\\\n| Nickel | 20 micrograms per litre |  |\\\\n| Nitrate (NO3) | 50 milligrams per litre | You also need to divide concentration of nitrate in milligrams per litre by 50. Add this to the concentration of nitrite in milligrams per litre. Divide it by 3 - it must not be more than 1. |\\\\n| Nitrite (NO2) | 0.5 milligrams per litre | You also need to divide concentration of nitrate in milligrams per litre by 50. Add this to the concentration of nitrite in milligrams per litre. Divide it by 3 - it must not be more than 1. |\\\\n| Polycyclic aromatic hydrocarbons | 0.1 micrograms per litre | This means the total of all individual polycyclic aromatic hydrocarbons found and measured during your testing should not be more than 0.10 micrograms per litre |\\\\n| Selenium | 10 micrograms per litre |  |\\\\n| Tetrachloroethene and trichloroethene | 10 micrograms per litre | This means the total of tetrachloroethene and trichloroethene combined should not be more than 10 micrograms per litre |\\\\n| Trichloromethanes | 100 micrograms per litre | This means the total of all individual trichloromethanes should not be more than 100 micrograms per litre |\\\\n\\\\n#### Chemical limits: special conditions for acrylamide, epichlorohydrin and vinyl chloride\\\\n\\\\nYour water must not contain more than the maximum limits for these 3 chemicals.\\\\n\\\\n| Chemical | Maximum limit |\\\\n| --- | --- |\\\\n| Acrylamide | 0.1 micrograms per litre |\\\\n| Epichlorohydrin | 0.1 micrograms per litre |\\\\n| Vinyl chloride | 0.5 micrograms per litre |\\\\n\\\\nIf there\\\\u2019s any risk of the water exceeding these limits, you must sample and test the water. However, you do not need to test the the water if you and the local authority are satisfied that:\\\\n\\\\n* your water has not come into contact with equipment made using acrylamide, epichlorohydrin and vinyl chloride\\\\n* you\\\\u2019ve not used any flocculants containing these 3 chemicals\\\\n\\\\nYou can demonstrate to the local authority that your water does not contain residues of these chemicals over the limits by providing either a manufacturer\\\\u2019s:\\\\n\\\\n* relevant certificate of conformity\\\\n* declaration of conformity\\\\n* declaration of performance\\\\n\\\\n#### Chemical limits: pesticides\\\\n\\\\nTest your water to make sure it complies with the following limits.\\\\n\\\\nFor your initial testing, take samples at source.\\\\n\\\\n| Pesticide | Maximum limit | Details |\\\\n| --- | --- | --- |\\\\n| Aldrin | 0.03 micrograms per litre |  |\\\\n| Dieldrin | 0.03 micrograms per litre |  |\\\\n| Heptachlor | 0.03 micrograms per litre |  |\\\\n| Heptachlor epoxide | 0.03 micrograms per litre |  |\\\\n| Other individual pesticides | 0.1 micrograms per litre | You only need to test for pesticides that are likely to be present in the water. The maximum of 0.1 micrograms per litre applies to each individual pesticide you test for. |\\\\n| Total pesticides | 0.5 micrograms per litre | Total of all pesticides you find should not equal more than 0.5 micrograms per litre |\\\\n\\\\n### Microbiological limits\\\\n\\\\nYour water must be free of parasites and bacteria that cause disease.\\\\n\\\\nTest your water to make sure it complies with the following limits.\\\\n\\\\nFor your initial testing, take samples at source.\\\\n\\\\n| Bacteria | Maximum limit |\\\\n| --- | --- |\\\\n| Escherichia coli | 0 per 250 ml |\\\\n| Pseudomonas aeruginosa | 0 per 250 ml |\\\\n| Faecal streptococci | 0 per 250 ml |\\\\n| Sporulated sulphite-reducing anaerobes | 0 per 50 ml |\\\\n| Total viable colony count (TVC) after 72 hours at 22\\\\u00baC | 100 per ml |\\\\n| TVC after 24 hours at 37\\\\u00baC | 20 per ml |\\\\n\\\\n### Radioactive limits\\\\n\\\\nTest your water to make sure it complies with the following limits.\\\\n\\\\nFor your initial testing, take samples at source.\\\\n\\\\n| Test for | Concentration or value |\\\\n| --- | --- |\\\\n| Radon | 100 becquerels per litre |\\\\n| Tritium | 100 becquerels per litre |\\\\n| Indicative dose | 0.1 millisievert (a year) |\\\\n\\\\n## Labelling rules\\\\n\\\\nYou should put one of the following terms on your labelling:\\\\n\\\\n* \\\\u2018water\\\\u2019\\\\n* \\\\u2018drinking water\\\\u2019\\\\n\\\\nYou must not use any of these terms:\\\\n\\\\n* natural mineral water\\\\n* mineral water\\\\n* spring water\\\\n\\\\n### Brand names\\\\n\\\\nYou can give your water a brand name.\\\\n\\\\nHowever, you must not mislead consumers about your water\\\\u2019s origin when you use branding. For example, you must not call it \\\\u2018Somerset Hills water\\\\u2019 when the water comes from Devon.\\\\n\\\\nYou also must not suggest the water has properties that it does not possess. For example, you must not call it \\\\u2018Welsh Mountain Water\\\\u2019 when you\\\\u2019re collecting the water from a reservoir.\\\\n\\\\n## When you\\\\u2019re allowed to start producing and marketing your bottled drinking water\\\\n\\\\nThe local authority will:\\\\n\\\\n* check your testing records\\\\n* make sure you\\\\u2019ve understood and complied with all the rules\\\\n\\\\nWhen they\\\\u2019re satisfied that your bottled drinking water meets the rules, they\\\\u2019ll register your business and confirm it in writing.\\\\n\\\\nOnce you\\\\u2019ve received this, you can start to produce and market your bottled drinking water.\\\\n\\\\n## Updates to this page\\\\n\\\\nPublished 28 May 2020\\\\n\\\\n## Sign up for emails or print this page\\\\n\\\\nGet emails about this page\\\\n\\\\nPrint this page\\\\n\\\\n[Contents](#contents)\\\\n\\\\n## Related content\\\\n\\\\n## Is this page useful?\\\\n\\\\n* [Maybe](/contact/govuk)\\\\n* Yes this page is useful\\\\n* No this page is not useful\\\\n\\\\nThank you for your feedback\\\\n\\\\nReport a problem with this page\\\\n\\\\n## Help us improve GOV.UK\\\\n\\\\nDo not include personal or financial information like your National Insurance number or credit card details.\\\\n\\\\nThis field is for robots only. Connect with us for all things health.\\\\n\\\\nSubscribe\\\\n\\\\n[Nutrition](https://www.healthline.com/nutrition)Evidence Based\\\\n\\\\n# What Is Ozonated Water, and Can You Drink It?\\\\n\\\\n![](https://i0.wp.com/post.healthline.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/Adrienne-Seitz-500x500-Bio.png?w=105&h=105)\\\\n\\\\nMedically reviewed by Adrienne Seitz, MS, RD, LDN \\\\u2014 Written by Fatima Hallal, APD  on October 6, 2021\\\\n\\\\nOzonated water refers to water that has been treated with ozone gas.\\\\n\\\\nIts proponents claim that it offers benefits in both clinical and industrial spaces, from preventing cancer and fighting free radicals in the body to supporting dental health and preserving food safety.\\\\n\\\\nHowever, recent studies on the topic are lacking, so it\\\\u2019s difficult to evaluate all of the claims about ozonated water.\\\\n\\\\nThis article explores the evidence on ozonated water, including how it\\\\u2019s made, its uses, its benefits, and its potential downsides.\\\\n\\\\n ![A glass of water sits on a table next to an ozonator.](https://i0.wp.com/post.healthline.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/10/glass-of-water-ozonator-oxygen-pump-generator-1296x728-header.jpg?w=1155&h=1528)[Share on Pinterest](https://www.pinterest.com/pin/create/button/?url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.healthline.com%2Fnutrition%2Fozonated-water&media=https%3A%2F%2Fpost.healthline.com%2Fwp-content%2Fuploads%2F2021%2F10%2Fglass-of-water-ozonator-oxygen-pump-generator-1296x728-header.jpg&description=Ozonated%20Water%3A%20Nutrition%2C%20Benefits%2C%20Downsides \\\\"Share on Pinterest\\\\")\\\\n\\\\nZenith Pictures/Shutterstock\\\\n\\\\n## What is ozonated water?\\\\n\\\\nOzone is a colorless and odorless gas comprising three oxygen atoms. In the gas form, ozone is an unstable molecule that can cause [damage to the lungs](https://www.healthline.com/nutrition/lung-cleansing-foods) when inhaled ([1](https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/25054009/)).\\\\n\\\\nWhen ozone is dissolved in water, the water becomes ozonated and is believed to have some therapeutic effects, including [antioxidant](https://www.healthline.com/nutrition/foods-high-in-antioxidants) and antimicrobial properties and use in dental therapy, cancer treatment, and food safety techniques ([2](https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/22470237/)).\\\\n\\\\nHowever, most of the studies on ozonated water are outdated, and newer research is needed.\\\\n\\\\n> **Summary**\\\\n>\\\\n> When ozone is dissolved in water, it becomes ozonated water. Ozonated water is thought to have therapeutic benefits that range from fighting cancer to keeping food fresh.\\\\n\\\\n## How it\\\\u2019s made\\\\n\\\\nMaking ozonated water involves filling a cylinder with [purified water](https://www.healthline.com/nutrition/purified-vs-distilled-vs-regular-water) while an ozone gas mixture bubbles through it continuously. This occurs for at least 5 minutes until maximum saturation has taken place. Then, the ozone gas will have fully dissolved into the water ([3](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC7498877/?report=classic)).\\\\n\\\\nIn its gas form, ozone may damage the respiratory system. Ozonated water is easier to handle than ozone gas itself. It may have both industrial and therapeutic uses ([4](https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/26506343/), [5](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC5674660/), [6](https://www.mdpi.com/2071-1050/10/12/4783)).\\\\n\\\\nIn past decades, [ozone was used to treat numerous ailments](https://www.healthline.com/health/ozone-therapy). Many historical applications were mostly anecdotal and not based on scientific literature, but some claims have been scientifically studied ([5](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC5674660/), [7](http://ozoneinmedicine.com/med03.pdf)).\\\\n\\\\n> **Summary**\\\\n>\\\\n> Ozonated water is made by continuously bubbling ozone gas into purified water. In the gas form, it may have respiratory consequences. However, ozonated water shows potential in the therapeutic space.\\\\n\\\\n## Benefits of ozonated water\\\\n\\\\nOver the past 2 decades, numerous studies have investigated the effects of using ozonated water to support health.\\\\n\\\\nHere are some potential benefits of using ozonated water.\\\\n\\\\nCancer treatment and prevention\\\\n\\\\nCancer treatment can be quite complex. Sometimes, popular therapies like chemotherapy and radiation therapy may not effectively target the tumor ([8](https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/11181773/)).\\\\n\\\\nResearch from the early 2000s found that ozonated water may enhance the efficacy of [chemotherapy](https://www.healthline.com/nutrition/foods-for-chemo) drugs in targeting tumors. However, these findings were based on a rat study, and the treatment has not yet been tested in humans ([8](https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/11181773/)).\\\\n\\\\nAnother study from the early 2000s looked at the risk of developing [bladder cancer](https://www.healthline.com/health/bladder-cancer/bladder-cancer-diet-and-nutrition) in adults who drank ozonated water compared with chlorinated water. Both techniques are used to disinfect water, preventing the growth of unsafe bacteria and microbes ([9](https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/15308961/)).\\\\n\\\\nBased on the results of this study, the risk of developing bladder cancer was lower in those who consumed ozonated water ([9](https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/15308961/)).\\\\n\\\\nHowever, more recent and longer-term studies are needed to support these claims.\\\\n\\\\nDental therapy\\\\n\\\\nOzone may be used as a treatment option within dentistry, according to more recent research. Some uses include clearing bad bacteria from the mouth and promoting the healing of oral wounds ([10](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC3276005/), [11](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S2352003516300260)).\\\\n\\\\nOne study tested the efficacy of ozonated water on tooth decay as an alternative to a chlorhexidine mouth rinse. It included 23 adults who had salivary samples taken at 7 and 14 days of continued use of ozonated water ([12](https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/28893032/)).\\\\n\\\\nResults showed a significant decrease in *Mutans Streptococci*, a bacterium found on teeth that increases the risk of [tooth decay](https://www.healthline.com/nutrition/foods-that-damage-teeth) ([12](https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/28893032/)).\\\\n\\\\nAnother study found that applying ozonated water to an oral wound sped the healing process by increasing cell turnover ([11](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S2352003516300260)).\\\\n\\\\nAntioxidant and antimicrobial\\\\n\\\\nOzone is considered an oxidant, meaning it\\\\u2019s a free-radical-forming substance. It\\\\u2019s an unstable molecule that may damage cells in the body.\\\\n\\\\nExposure to ozone gas may trigger a stress response in the body. This response may activate the production of numerous antioxidants that help clear free radicals from the body ([13](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC5674660/)).\\\\n\\\\nA case study of a 62-year-old woman showed the effects of using ozonated water, in addition to antibiotics, to treat a [urinary tract infection](https://www.healthline.com/nutrition/diet-and-utis-foods-to-avoid-with-a-uti) (UTI). Ozonated water was administered into the urinary tract 3 times over 1 week ([14](https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/24403204/)).\\\\n\\\\nThe patient [recovered from the UTI](https://www.healthline.com/nutrition/uti-home-remedies), and no reinfection was documented in the period leading up to the 4-month follow-up ([14](https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/24403204/)).\\\\n\\\\nNevertheless, more research is needed, as this study only looked at one individual who was taking antibiotics in addition to the ozonated water.\\\\n\\\\nExposure to ozonated water may speed the cell repair process, reducing bacteria and symptoms related to urinary tract infections ([14](https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/24403204/)).\\\\n\\\\nIn addition to its antioxidant properties, ozonated water may increase microbes\\\\u2019 sensitivity to antibiotic treatment ([15](https://www.mdpi.com/2071-1050/10/12/4783)).\\\\n\\\\nFood safety and water purification\\\\n\\\\nOzone\\\\u2019s antibacterial properties and ability to destroy industrial impurities have made it a potentially valuable alternative to chlorine ([7](http://ozoneinmedicine.com/med03.pdf), [15](https://www.mdpi.com/2071-1050/10/12/4783)).\\\\n\\\\nIn 1901, one city in Germany and another in France were the first to implement the use of ozone to [purify drinking water](https://www.healthline.com/nutrition/how-to-filter-water). Today, at least 3,000 cities use ozone to purify their drinking water ([7](http://ozoneinmedicine.com/med03.pdf)).\\\\n\\\\nIn 1995, the United States Food and Drug Administration (FDA) listed ozone as \\\\u201cgenerally recognized as safe\\\\u201d in regards to bottled water and coming into contact with food ([15](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC8000956/)).\\\\n\\\\nAccording to both older and recent studies, ozonated water may be used to [wash fresh vegetables](https://www.healthline.com/nutrition/washing-vegetables) to reduce bacteria on their surface and enhance preservation. However, its use should occur within a controlled environment ([15](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC8000956/), [16](https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/15998129/)[)](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC8000956/).\\\\n\\\\n## Potential downsides\\\\n\\\\nOzone gas is considered a pollutant, which produces an [inflammatory](https://www.healthline.com/nutrition/13-anti-inflammatory-foods) response that may cause damage to the airways when inhaled ([17](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC6834528/)).\\\\n\\\\nEven short-term exposure is known to exacerbate respiratory symptoms in adults and children ([17](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC6834528/)).\\\\n\\\\nAdditionally, much older studies suggest that ozone may contribute to low birth weight if exposure takes place during the second or third trimester ([18](https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/16263524/), [19](https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/7376198/)).\\\\n\\\\nHowever, more recent studies are needed to support this claim and understand the mechanism through which this might occur.\\\\n\\\\nMost studies evaluated the effects of ozone gas rather than the effects of ozonated water. Currently, there does not appear to be any research linking respiratory symptoms or low birth weights to ozonated water.\\\\n\\\\nOzone gas may impose risks if not handled by an expert, but those risks aren\\\\u2019t fully understood.\\\\n\\\\n> **Summary**\\\\n>\\\\n> Ozonated water has antibacterial and antioxidant-promoting properties. If handled safely, it may help prevent tooth decay, minimize bladder cancer risk, purify drinking water, and improve the effectiveness of cancer treatment.\\\\n\\\\n## The bottom line\\\\n\\\\nWhile ozone gas may pose some health risks, ozonated water continues to demonstrate therapeutic potential.\\\\n\\\\nThe FDA considers ozonated water to be safe when it comes to drinking water and coming into contact with food.\\\\n\\\\nIn a controlled environment, such as in industrial water plants or under medical supervision, there\\\\u2019s evidence that ozonated water may be safe to drink and use in some medical therapies.\\\\n\\\\nHowever, more research is needed to support the safety and benefits of ozonated water for oral consumption.\\\\n\\\\n### Just one thing\\\\n\\\\n*Try this today*: If you are looking for an alternative drink to plain water, you may want to consider trying sparkling water or getting creative with fruit-infused water.\\\\n\\\\n### How we reviewed this article:\\\\n\\\\nHistory\\\\n\\\\nShare this article\\\\n\\\\n### Evidence Based\\\\n\\\\nThis article is based on scientific evidence, written by [experts](https://www.healthline.com/nutrition-team) and fact checked by experts.\\\\n\\\\nOur team of licensed nutritionists and dietitians strive to be objective, unbiased, honest and to present both sides of the argument.\\\\n\\\\nThis article contains scientific references. The numbers in the parentheses (1, 2, 3) are clickable links to peer-reviewed scientific papers.\\\\n\\\\n![](https://i0.wp.com/post.healthline.com/wp-content/uploads/2022/01/Adrienne-Seitz-500x500-Bio.png?w=105&h=105)\\\\n\\\\nMedically reviewed by Adrienne Seitz, MS, RD, LDN \\\\u2014 Written by Fatima Hallal, APD  on October 6, 2021\\\\n\\\\n## related stories\\\\n\\\\n* [What Is CBD Water, and Should You Drink It?](https://www.healthline.com/nutrition/cbd-water?utm_source=ReadNext)\\\\n* [Does Sparkling Water Hydrate You?](https://www.healthline.com/nutrition/does-sparkling-water-hydrate-you?utm_source=ReadNext)\\\\n* [Is There a Best Time to Drink Water?](https://www.healthline.com/nutrition/best-time-to-drink-water?utm_source=ReadNext)\\\\n* [Does Mineral Water Have Health Benefits?](https://www.healthline.com/nutrition/mineral-water-benefits?utm_source=ReadNext)\\\\n* [9 Types of Drinking Water and How to Choose the Best Option](https://www.healthline.com/health/food-nutrition/nine-types-of-drinking-water?utm_source=ReadNext)\\\\n\\\\n\\\\u00a9 2026 Healthline Media LLC. Accepted 2015 Oct 12; Collection date 2015 Oct.\\\\n\\\\n\\\\u00a9 2015 by the authors; licensee MDPI, Basel, Switzerland.\\\\n\\\\nThis article is an open access article distributed under the terms and conditions of the Creative Commons Attribution license (<http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by/4.0/>).\\\\n\\\\n[PMC Copyright notice](/about/copyright/)\\\\n\\\\nPMCID: PMC4632793\\\\u00a0\\\\u00a0PMID: [26506343](https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/26506343/)\\\\n\\\\n## Abstract\\\\n\\\\nOzonated water is easier to handle than ozone gas. However, there have been no previous reports on the biological effects of ozonated water. We conducted a study on the safety of ozonated water and its anti-tumor effects using a tumor-bearing mouse model and normal controls. Local administration of ozonated water (208 mM) was not associated with any detrimental effects in normal tissues. On the other hand, local administration of ozonated water (20.8, 41.6, 104, or 208 mM) directly into the tumor tissue induced necrosis and inhibited proliferation of tumor cells. There was no significant difference in the number of terminal deoxynucleotidyl transferase-mediated deoxyuridine triphosphate-biotin nick-end labeling (TUNEL)-positive cells following administration of ozonated water. The size of the necrotic areas was dependent on the concentration of ozonated water. These results indicate that ozonated water does not affect normal tissue and damages only the tumor tissue by selectively inducing necrosis. There is a possibility that it exerts through the production of reaction oxygen species (ROS). In addition, the induction of necrosis rather than apoptosis is very useful in tumor immunity. Based on these results, we believe that administration of ozonated water is a safe and potentially simple adjunct or alternative to existing antineoplastic treatments.\\\\n\\\\n**Keywords:** ozone, ozonated water, anti-tumor effect, reactive oxygen species\\\\n\\\\n## 1. Introduction\\\\n\\\\nOzone is an active form of oxygen consisting of three oxygen atoms that is generated from diatomic oxygen by ultraviolet light and high voltage. Ozone gas is clear, colorless, and smells slightly like grass. Moreover, it is very unstable and decomposes into diatomic oxygen within a few hours in air, and has a very short half-life of approximately 30 min in water [[1](#B1-ijms-16-25108)]. Ozone therapy has been receiving increasing attention in Europe in recent years. In this regard, major autohemotherapy (MAH), the main form of ozone therapy, is known for its beneficial effects as adjunct therapy for cardiovascular disease, infection, cancer, rheumatoid arthritis, and osteoarthritis [[2](#B2-ijms-16-25108)]. In MAH, the patient\\\\u2019s blood is mixed with ozone gas before being retransfused. A previous report indicated that MAH in patients with cancer may improve tumor hypoxia and enhance sensitivity to both chemotherapy and radiation therapy [[3](#B3-ijms-16-25108)]. In a clinical setting, a combination of radiation therapy and MAH or rectal administration of an ozone/oxygen gas mixture achieved the same effects as a combination of radiation therapy and chemotherapy in preventing progression of head and neck cancer [[4](#B4-ijms-16-25108)]. However, there have been no reports on the direct effects of ozone gas on tumor cells *in vivo*, and to the best of our knowledge, only the *in vitro* effects have been studied [[5](#B5-ijms-16-25108),[6](#B6-ijms-16-25108)].\\\\n\\\\nWhile ozone gas therapy has many advantages, it has not been widely used in medical settings since ozone gas is toxic to the respiratory tract of the lung [[7](#B7-ijms-16-25108),[8](#B8-ijms-16-25108)]. In contrast, ozonated water which means the water dissolved ozone gas has no reported side effects, and it is much easier to handle than ozone gas. Despite these advantages, however, ozonated water has not found widespread application in medicine because it is difficult to obtain an exact concentration of ozone in water. Recently, a device has been developed that can produce ozonated water to an exact concentration [[9](#B9-ijms-16-25108)]. We made use of this device to study the safety and anti-tumor effects of ozonated water through the administration of ozonated water to normal and tumor-bearing mice.\\\\n\\\\n## 2. Results and Discussion\\\\n\\\\n### 2.1. Effects of Administration of Ozonated Water into Normal Tissue\\\\n\\\\nIn the intraperitoneal administration (IP) group, no abnormalities such as edema of the organs or ascites were observed macroscopically ([Figure 1](#ijms-16-25108-f001)A). No abnormalities were observed in any of the examined organs (liver, spleen, kidney, and small intestine) on histopathological examination ([Figure 2](#ijms-16-25108-f002)A\\\\u2013D). In the subcutaneous administration (SC) group, no subcutaneous abnormalities were observed macroscopically ([Figure 1](#ijms-16-25108-f001)B). In the intramuscular administration (IM) group, no abnormalities such as claudication were observed in any mice. No abnormalities were observed on histopathological examination either ([Figure 2](#ijms-16-25108-f002)E).\\\\n\\\\n#### Figure 1.\\\\n\\\\n[![Figure 1](https://cdn.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/blobs/9d68/4632793/5d0cb1a4ccd9/ijms-16-25108-g001.jpg)](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/core/lw/2.0/html/tileshop_pmc/tileshop_pmc_inline.html?title=Click%20on%20image%20to%20zoom&p=PMC3&id=4632793_ijms-16-25108-g001.jpg)\\\\n\\\\n[Open in a new tab](figure/ijms-16-25108-f001/)\\\\n\\\\nMacroscopic images of the organs in the abdominal cavity (**A**) and subcutaneous tissue (**B**).\\\\n\\\\n#### Figure 2.\\\\n\\\\n[![Figure 2](https://cdn.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/blobs/9d68/4632793/d4d617cb3939/ijms-16-25108-g002.jpg)](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/core/lw/2.0/html/tileshop_pmc/tileshop_pmc_inline.html?title=Click%20on%20image%20to%20zoom&p=PMC3&id=4632793_ijms-16-25108-g002.jpg)\\\\n\\\\n[Open in a new tab](figure/ijms-16-25108-f002/)\\\\n\\\\nHistological images of normal tissues of the liver (**A**), small intestine (**B**), spleen (**C**), kidney (**D**) and muscle (**E**) 24 h after the last administration of ozonated water. All sections were observed (100\\\\u00d7) after staining with hematoxylin and eosin.\\\\n\\\\n### 2.2. Concentration and Time-Dependent Effects of Ozonated Water after Local Injection in Tumor Tissue\\\\n\\\\nNecrosis was observed around the injection site in all groups except for the non-treatment (NT) group. In the O3-1, O3-2, and O3-3 groups, nuclei were not observed in the tumor cells in the centermost areas of necrosis. Pyknotic nuclei were abundant at the edges of the necrotic region ([Figure 3](#ijms-16-25108-f003)). In the O3-3 group, the area of necrosis was particularly broad and the area in which nuclei were not observed in the tumor cells was larger compared to the O3-1 and O3-2 groups ([Figure 3](#ijms-16-25108-f003)E). In the O3-4/1 day, O3-4/3 day, and O3-4/7 day groups, necrosis in the tumor tissues was observed to about the same extent as that in the other ozonated water groups ([Figure 4](#ijms-16-25108-f004)). However, viable tumor cells were observed in the necrotic area in the O3-4/7 day group ([Figure 4](#ijms-16-25108-f004)E). In the NT and local administration of sterile distilled water (solvent control) into the tumor tissue (C) groups, many pyknotic nuclei were seen in the necrotic areas ([Figure 5](#ijms-16-25108-f005)). In the NT group, pyknotic nuclei were more frequent in the centermost regions of tumor tissue compared with other groups ([Figure 5](#ijms-16-25108-f005)A,B).\\\\n\\\\n#### Figure 3.\\\\n\\\\n[![Figure 3](https://cdn.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/blobs/9d68/4632793/2c486397019a/ijms-16-25108-g003.jpg)](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/core/lw/2.0/html/tileshop_pmc/tileshop_pmc_inline.html?title=Click%20on%20image%20to%20zoom&p=PMC3&id=4632793_ijms-16-25108-g003.jpg)\\\\n\\\\n[Open in a new tab](figure/ijms-16-25108-f003/)\\\\n\\\\nHistological images of tumors 1 day after administration of 20.8, 41.6, or 104 mM ozonated water. Low magnification (40\\\\u00d7): (**A**,**C**,**E**); High magnification (400\\\\u00d7): (**B**,**D**,**F**). The concentration of ozonated water was 20.8 mM (**A**,**B**); 41.6 mM (**C**,**D**); or 104 mM (**E**,**F**). All sections were stained with hematoxylin and eosin. N: necrotic area; L: viable tumor area; arrow: site of injection; arrowhead: pyknotic nuclei.\\\\n\\\\n#### Figure 4.\\\\n\\\\n[![Figure 4](https://cdn.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/blobs/9d68/4632793/44f00b7178f0/ijms-16-25108-g004.jpg)](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/core/lw/2.0/html/tileshop_pmc/tileshop_pmc_inline.html?title=Click%20on%20image%20to%20zoom&p=PMC3&id=4632793_ijms-16-25108-g004.jpg)\\\\n\\\\n[Open in a new tab](figure/ijms-16-25108-f004/)\\\\n\\\\nHistological images of tumors after administration of 208 mM ozonated water. the O3-4/1 day group is (**A**,**B**); O3-4/3 day group is (**C**,**D**); O3-4/7 day group is (**E**,**F**). Low magnification (40\\\\u00d7): (**A**,**C**,**E**); High magnification (400\\\\u00d7): (**B**,**D**,**F**). All sections were stained with hematoxylin and eosin. N: necrotic area; L: viable tumor area; arrow: site of injection; arrowhead: pyknotic nuclei.\\\\n\\\\n#### Figure 5.\\\\n\\\\n[![Figure 5](https://cdn.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/blobs/9d68/4632793/7ba2a70da3b1/ijms-16-25108-g005a.jpg)](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/core/lw/2.0/html/tileshop_pmc/tileshop_pmc_inline.html?title=Click%20on%20image%20to%20zoom&p=PMC3&id=4632793_ijms-16-25108-g005a.jpg)\\\\n\\\\n[![Figure 5](https://cdn.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/blobs/9d68/4632793/e529e5afa04a/ijms-16-25108-g005b.jpg)](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/core/lw/2.0/html/tileshop_pmc/tileshop_pmc_inline.html?title=Click%20on%20image%20to%20zoom&p=PMC3&id=4632793_ijms-16-25108-g005b.jpg)\\\\n\\\\n[Open in a new tab](figure/ijms-16-25108-f005/)\\\\n\\\\nHistological images of tumors that were either untreated or administered sterile distilled water, after 24 h. Non-treated (**A**,**B**); treated with sterile distilled water (**C**,**D**). Low magnification (40\\\\u00d7): (**A**,**C**); High magnification (400\\\\u00d7): (**B**,**D**). All sections were stained with hematoxylin and eosin. N: necrotic area; L: viable tumor area; arrow: site of injection; arrowhead: pyknotic nuclei.\\\\n\\\\n### 2.3. The Effects of Local Administration of Ozonated Water on Tumor Growth\\\\n\\\\nThe tumor growth rate in the O3 group (9.9 \\\\u00b1 2.7 mm3/day) was significantly decreased compared to that of the NT group (55.3 \\\\u00b1 16.0 mm3/day) (*p* < 0.05, [Figure 6](#ijms-16-25108-f006)). The tumor growth rate in the C group was 32.9 \\\\u00b1 8.1 mm3/day. No significant difference was seen between the O3 and C groups. However, a tendency was observed toward decreased rates of tumor growth in the O3 group compared to the C group.\\\\n\\\\n#### Figure 6.\\\\n\\\\n[![Figure 6](https://cdn.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/blobs/9d68/4632793/57c87c2dc936/ijms-16-25108-g006.jpg)](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/core/lw/2.0/html/tileshop_pmc/tileshop_pmc_inline.html?title=Click%20on%20image%20to%20zoom&p=PMC3&id=4632793_ijms-16-25108-g006.jpg)\\\\n\\\\n[Open in a new tab](figure/ijms-16-25108-f006/)\\\\n\\\\nThe effect of local administration of ozonated water on rates of tumor growth. The data represent the mean \\\\u00b1 SE; *n* = 5 in the NT and C groups, *n* = 6 in the O3 group. \\\\\\\\* *p* < 0.05 compared to the NT group by using the Tukey\\\\u2013Kramer test. NT: non-treatment group; C: local administration of sterile distilled water group; O3: local administration of ozonated water group.\\\\n\\\\nThe area of tumor necrosis was significantly increased in the O3 group ((26.0% \\\\u00b1 5.2%)/field), compared to that in the NT group ((8.3% \\\\u00b1 1.5%)/field) (*p* < 0.05, [Figure 7](#ijms-16-25108-f007)). Meanwhile, the area of tumor necrosis in the C group was (18.5% \\\\u00b1 2.6%)/field, with no significant difference from that in the O3 group. However, a tendency toward increased tumor necrosis was seen in the O3 group compared to the C group. The number of TUNEL-positive cells in the three groups did not significantly differ ([Table 1](#ijms-16-25108-t001)).\\\\n\\\\n#### Figure 7.\\\\n\\\\n[![Figure 7](https://cdn.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/blobs/9d68/4632793/1b88832e78da/ijms-16-25108-g007.jpg)](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/core/lw/2.0/html/tileshop_pmc/tileshop_pmc_inline.html?title=Click%20on%20image%20to%20zoom&p=PMC3&id=4632793_ijms-16-25108-g007.jpg)\\\\n\\\\n[Open in a new tab](figure/ijms-16-25108-f007/)\\\\n\\\\nThe effect of local administration of ozonated water on size of areas of tumor necrosis. The data represent the mean \\\\u00b1 SE; *n* = 5 in the NT and C groups, *n* = 6 in the O3 group. \\\\\\\\* *p* < 0.05 compared to the NT group by using the Tukey\\\\u2013Kramer test. NT: non-treatment group; C: local administration of sterile distilled water group; O3: local administration of ozonated water group.\\\\n\\\\n#### Table 1.\\\\n\\\\nThe number of erminal deoxynucleotidyl transferase-mediated deoxyuridine triphosphate-biotin nick-end labeling (TUNEL) positive cells in tumors.\\\\n\\\\n| Staining | NT | C | O3 |\\\\n| --- | --- | --- | --- |\\\\n| TUNEL positive cells (cells/field) | 7.92 \\\\u00b1 0.63 | 9.24 \\\\u00b1 0.61 | 9.34 \\\\u00b1 1.02 |\\\\n\\\\n[Open in a new tab](table/ijms-16-25108-t001/)\\\\n\\\\nThe data represent the mean \\\\u00b1 SE; *n* = 5 in the NT and C groups, *n* = 6 in the O3 group. There was no significant difference between the three groups. NT: non-treatment group; C: local administration of sterile distilled water group; O3: local administration of ozonated water group.\\\\n\\\\n### 2.4. Discussion\\\\n\\\\nIt has been shown that ozonated water has antibacterial effects [[10](#B10-ijms-16-25108),[11](#B11-ijms-16-25108)]. Ozmen *et al.* reported that \\\\u201cozonated saline was effective as irrigation for treating experimental peritonitis rats\\\\u201d [[12](#B12-ijms-16-25108)]. To the best of our knowledge, the side-effects of ozonated water have not yet been reported. In the present study, it was found that ozonated water did not affect normal tissue. Moreover, ozonated water was found to inhibit tumor growth through the induction of necrosis of tumor cells. During the experimented period, no detrimental effects were observed following local administration of ozonated water. These results indicate that administration of ozonated water has low toxicity and is safe and very useful in anti-tumor treatment. However, these results are only indicative of a short-term effect. Therefore, further information regarding the potential long-term effects of ozonated water is needed.\\\\n\\\\nNecrosis of the tumor cells was observed following local injection of ozonated water directly into the tumor tissues. Moreover, the tumor growth rate was significantly decreased and there was a significant increase in the tumor necrotic area. However, there were no significant differences among the three groups in the number of TUNEL-positive cells. These results indicate that local administration of ozonated water does not induce apoptosis, although it does act directly on the tumor cells. It has been reported that ozone gas directly inhibits neoplastic cell growth in the neuroblastoma SK-N-SH cell line *in vitro* by modulating the cell cycle [[6](#B6-ijms-16-25108)]. However, to the best of our knowledge, no previous studies have investigated the direct effects of ozone on tumor tissue *in vivo*. This report is the first regarding the direct effects of ozone on tumor tissue.\\\\n\\\\nIn this study, the tendency that the tumor growth rate is decreased and the area of tumor necrosis is increased was observed in C group. However, these data were not significantly compared to that in NT group. We think that it was induced by physical injury when water and/or osmotic pressure was injected.\\\\n\\\\nMany tumor cells have few antioxidant materials, such as superoxide dismutase (SOD), catalase, and glutathione peroxidase, in comparison with normal cells [[13](#B13-ijms-16-25108)]. Therefore, the tumor cells are greatly affected by reactive oxygen species (ROS). It is well known that in a variety of anticancer agents, such as adriamycin and *cis*-diamminedichloroplatinum (II), ROS play important roles in the cytotoxic effects on tumor cells [[14](#B14-ijms-16-25108),[15](#B15-ijms-16-25108)]. High-dose ascorbic acid therapy controls the growth of aggressive tumors by producing ROS [[16](#B16-ijms-16-25108)]. ROS can interact with numerous cellular components, including DNA, lipids, and proteins [[17](#B17-ijms-16-25108)]. The consequences of these interactions include losses of cell integrity, enzyme function, and genomic stability [[18](#B18-ijms-16-25108),[19](#B19-ijms-16-25108)]. When ozone is administered *in vivo*, it is well known that ROS such as hydrogen peroxide (H2O2) are generated [[20](#B20-ijms-16-25108)]. Therefore, the anti-tumor mechanism of ozonated water is likely to also be the cell injury caused by ROS. It will be necessary to verify the association between ROS and anti-tumor effects of ozonated water using ROS inhibitors.\\\\n\\\\nThe necrotic cell releases danger signals such as deoxyribonucleic acid (DNA), high mobility group box 1 protein (HMGB1), and uric acid [[21](#B21-ijms-16-25108),[22](#B22-ijms-16-25108),[23](#B23-ijms-16-25108)]. On the other hand, the apoptotic cell does not release these signals [[22](#B22-ijms-16-25108),[24](#B24-ijms-16-25108)]. An antigen-presenting cell (APC), particularly the dendritic cell (DC), matures following stimulation by cytokines and danger signals, after uptake of the tumor antigen. In conditions in which danger signals are lacking, APCs cannot mature and activate T cells. Therefore, the growth of tumors may be promoted under the non-existence of danger signals. In a previous report, a decrease in metastasis and an extension in the duration of survival were observed in a mouse tumor necrosis model compared to a mouse tumor apoptosis model [[25](#B25-ijms-16-25108)]. Therefore, the induction of necrosis rather than apoptosis by administration of ozonated water is very useful in tumor immunity.\\\\n\\\\nIt has been reported that the production of several cytokines including interferon (IFN)-\\\\u03b1, IFN-\\\\u03b2, and IFN-\\\\u03b3, interleukin (IL)-1, IL-2, tumor necrosis factor (TNF)-\\\\u03b1, and granulocyte-macrophage colony-stimulating factor was induced after human blood, heparinized platelet-rich plasma, and Ficoll-purified blood mononuclear cells were ozonated [[26](#B26-ijms-16-25108),[27](#B27-ijms-16-25108),[28](#B28-ijms-16-25108),[29](#B29-ijms-16-25108)]. Previous reports have indicated that cytokines inhibit both tumor growth and metastasis [[30](#B30-ijms-16-25108),[31](#B31-ijms-16-25108),[32](#B32-ijms-16-25108),[33](#B33-ijms-16-25108),[34](#B34-ijms-16-25108)]. Therefore, cytokines may also participate in the growth restraint of tumors. Further studies on the kinetics of these cytokines following administration of ozonated water will be needed to determine their roles in the antineoplastic activity of ozonated water.\\\\n\\\\nImportantly, the size of the necrotic area in the current study was dependent on the concentration of the ozonated water. Concentration-dependent growth inhibition has been reported *in vitro* in human cancer cells from lung, breast, and uterine tumors following treatment with ozone gas [[5](#B5-ijms-16-25108)]. Herein, when the observation time was extended, viable tumor cells were observed in the necrotic area in the O3-4/168 h group. This result indicates that a single administration of ozonated water cannot achieve complete destruction of tumor cells, and thus repeated administration is required.\\\\n\\\\n## 3. Experimental Section\\\\n\\\\n### 3.1. Preparation of Ozonated Water\\\\n\\\\nThe device producing ozonated water was provided by Sakuragawa Pump Co., Ltd., (Osaka, Japan). This device can produce ozonated water from O2 and water and can regulate the concentration of the dissolved O3. In all experiments, ozonated water was administered within 10 min after production.\\\\n\\\\n### 3.2. Animals\\\\n\\\\nBALB/c mice (4\\\\u20135 week-old, female) were purchased from CLEA Japan, Inc. (Osaka, Japan). All mice were maintained under conventional conditions. The study was carried out according to Tottori University animal experiment rule. The use of these animals and the procedures undertaken were approved by the Animal Research Committee of Tottori University (Permit Number: 13T4). All treatments were performed under anesthesia induced by inhalation of 3%\\\\u20135% isoflurane and all efforts were made to minimize suffering.\\\\n\\\\n### 3.3. Preparation of the Tumor-Bearing Mouse Model\\\\n\\\\nMouse cell line derived from mouse rectal cancer, Colon 26 (RCB2657), was obtained from by the RIKEN BioResource Center (BRC) through the National Bio-Resource Project of the MEXT (Ibaraki, Japan). The tumor-bearing mouse model was prepared as previously described, with slight modification [[35](#B35-ijms-16-25108)]. In brief, 1 \\\\u00d7 106 colon 26 cells (1 \\\\u00d7 107 cells/mL) were subcutaneously injected into the dorsal regions in BALB/c mice. Mice whose tumors grew to a diameter of 7\\\\u201310 mm were used in the experiments.\\\\n\\\\n### 3.4. Effects of Administration of Ozonated Water into Normal Tissue\\\\n\\\\nMice were randomized into three groups: intraperitoneal administration (IP) group, subcutaneous administration (SC) group, and intramuscular administration (IM) group. In the IP and SC groups, 1 mL of 208 \\\\u00b5M ozonated water was administered under anesthesia induced by inhalation of 3%\\\\u20135% isoflurane. In the IM group, 0.1 mL of 208 mM ozonated water was administered. Ozonated water was administered for three days. Twenty-four hours after the last administration, all mice were euthanized by cervical dislocation under anesthesia induced by inhalation of 3%\\\\u20135% isoflurane. Each organ, as well as samples of subcutaneous tissue and muscle, were observed macroscopically and fixed in 10% buffered formalin.\\\\n\\\\n### 3.5. Concentration and Time-Dependent Effects of Ozonated Water after Local Injection in Tumor Tissue\\\\n\\\\nMice were randomized into six groups: non-treatment (NT) group; local administration of sterile distilled water (solvent control) into the tumor tissue (C); local administration of 20.8 mM ozonated water into the tumor tissue (O3-1); local administration of 41.6 mM ozonated water into the tumor tissue (O3-2); local administration of 104 mM ozonated water into the tumor tissue (O3-3) (*n* = 3 in each group); and local administration of 208 mM ozonated water into the tumor tissue (O3-4) (*n* = 9). One milliliter of sterile distilled or ozonated water was administered under anesthesia induced by inhalation of 3%\\\\u20135% isoflurane. In the NT, C, O3-1, O3-2, and O3-3 groups, all mice were euthanized by cervical dislocation and the tumors were resected 24 h after administration. In the O3-4 group, all mice were euthanized by cervical dislocation and the tumors were resected one, three, and seven days after administration (O3-4/1 day, O3-4/3 day and O3-4/7 day groups, each *n* = 3). The tumors were fixed in 10% buffered formalin.\\\\n\\\\n### 3.6. The Effects of Local Administration of Ozonated Water on Tumor Growth\\\\n\\\\nMice were randomized into three groups: NT group (*n* = 5); local administration of sterile distilled water (solvent control) into the tumor tissue (C, *n* = 5); and local administration of ozonated water into the tumor tissue (O3, *n* = 6). The volumes of the tumor tissues were calculated as follows: (mediastinum \\\\u00d7 transverse line \\\\u00d7 depth \\\\u00d7 \\\\u03c0)/6 (mm3). After calculations of the tumor volumes, distilled water or 208 mM of ozonated water was locally administered into the tumor tissues (0.2 mL/head, day 1). After three days (day 4), a second local injection of distilled water or 208 mM ozonated water was given. On day 7, mice were euthanized by cervical dislocation under anesthesia induced by inhalation of 3%\\\\u20135% isoflurane. Based on the tumor volumes on days 1 and 7, the tumor growth rates were calculated as follows: (tumor volume on day 7 \\\\u2212 tumor volume on day 1)/7 (mm3/day). The tumors were fixed in 10% buffered formalin.\\\\n\\\\n### 3.7. Histological Evaluation and Image Analysis\\\\n\\\\nThin sections (5 \\\\u03bcm) were cut from each sample for histological observation after staining with hematoxylin and eosin. Each section was examined microscopically and quantitative digital morphometric analysis of necrotic areas was performed. The color wavelengths of the copied images were transformed into digital readings using the Lumina Vision software program (Mitani Corporation, Tokyo, Japan), which allows for quantification of the various color wavelengths with pixels as the unit of measurement. The percentage of necrosis in the tumor tissues was calculated by dividing the total pixel area of the necrotic area by the total pixel area corresponding to the total tumor tissue in the field of view [[35](#B35-ijms-16-25108)].\\\\n\\\\nApoptosis of the tumor tissues was investigated using terminal deoxynucleotidyl transferase-mediated deoxyuridine triphosphate-biotin nick-end labeling (TUNEL) staining. Staining was performed according to previously described methods [[36](#B36-ijms-16-25108)]. Each section was examined microscopically and the number of TUNEL-positive cells in each tumor was calculated. Cell counts were calculated in five fields, excluding necrotic regions, at 400\\\\u00d7 magnification using five mice in each group. The mean score of 25 fields was considered the number of TUNEL-positive cells in each group.\\\\n\\\\n### 3.8. Statistical Analysis\\\\n\\\\nData were expressed as the mean \\\\u00b1 standard error (SE). Statistical analyses were first performed using one-way analysis of variance (ANOVA) and followed and compared using the Tukey\\\\u2013Kramer test. A value of *p* < 0.05 was considered statistically significant.\\\\n\\\\n## 4. Conclusions\\\\n\\\\nIn this study, it is suggested that ozonated water has an anti-tumor effect. There is a possibility that it is exerted through the production of ROS. Moreover, ozonated water has low toxicity and is safe and easy to handle. On the other hand, ozone gas is dangerous and not easy to handle. This is because ozone gas is toxic to the respiratory tract of the lung [[7](#B7-ijms-16-25108),[8](#B8-ijms-16-25108)]. Administration of ozonated water is a safe and potentially simple adjunct or alternative to existing antineoplastic treatments.\\\\n\\\\n## Author Contributions\\\\n\\\\nKazuo Azuma, Tomohiro Imagawa and Yoshiharu Okamoto conceived and designed the experiments; Fumio Itoh contributed device; Kohei Kuroda, Takuro Mori and Kinya Kawamoto performed the experiments; Kohei Kuroda, Yusuke Murahata, Takeshi Tsuka, Norihiko Ito analysed the data; Kohei Kuroda wrote the manuscript; Kazuo Azuma, Tomohiro Osaki and Yoshiharu Okamoto performed correction and revision of the manuscript.\\\\n\\\\n## Conflicts of Interest\\\\n\\\\nThe authors declare no conflict of interest.\\\\n\\\\n## References\\\\n\\\\n* 1.Viebahn-Haensler R., Lee A.
